	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Incest</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Sexual activity between family members or close relatives</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the variable social, legal, religious, and cultural attitudes and sanctions concerning human sexual relations with close kin. For the biological act of reproducing with close kin, see <a href="/wiki/Inbreeding" title="Inbreeding">Inbreeding</a>. For the descriptive term for blood-related kin, see <a href="/wiki/Consanguinity" title="Consanguinity">Consanguinity</a>.</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Incest_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Incest (disambiguation)">Incest (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<p><b>Incest</b> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/ɛ/: &#39;e&#39; in &#39;dress&#39;">ɛ</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span></span>/</a></span></span> is <a href="/wiki/Human_sexual_activity" title="Human sexual activity">human sexual activity</a> between family members or close <a href="/wiki/Kinship" title="Kinship">relatives</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Incest1_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Incest1-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Incest2_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Incest2-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> This typically includes sexual activity between people in <a href="/wiki/Consanguinity" title="Consanguinity">consanguinity</a> (blood relations), and sometimes those related by <a href="/wiki/Affinity_(law)" title="Affinity (law)">affinity</a> (<a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">marriage</a> or <a href="/wiki/Stepfamily" title="Stepfamily">stepfamily</a>), <a href="/wiki/Adoption" title="Adoption">adoption</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clan" title="Clan">clan</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Lineage_(anthropology)" title="Lineage (anthropology)">lineage</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Incest_taboo" title="Incest taboo">incest taboo</a> is one of the most widespread of all cultural <a href="/wiki/Taboo" title="Taboo">taboos</a>, both in present and in past societies.<sup id="cite_ref-Bittles_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bittles-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Most modern societies have <a href="/wiki/Laws_regarding_incest" class="mw-redirect" title="Laws regarding incest">laws regarding incest</a> or social restrictions on closely consanguineous marriages.<sup id="cite_ref-Bittles_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bittles-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> In societies where it is illegal, consensual adult incest is seen by some as a <a href="/wiki/Victimless_crime" title="Victimless crime">victimless crime</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-spiegel_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spiegel-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wolf169_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wolf169-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Some cultures extend the incest taboo to relatives with no consanguinity such as <a href="/wiki/Milk_kinship" title="Milk kinship">milk-siblings</a>, step-siblings, and adoptive siblings, albeit sometimes with less intensity.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Third-degree relatives (such as half-aunt, half-nephew, first cousin) on average have 12.5% common genetic heritage, and sexual relations between them are viewed differently in various cultures, from being discouraged to being socially acceptable.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Children of incestuous relationships have been regarded as <a href="/wiki/Legitimacy_(family_law)" title="Legitimacy (family law)">illegitimate</a>, and are still so regarded in some societies today. In most cases, the parents did not have the option to marry to remove that status, as incestuous marriages were, and are, normally also prohibited.
</p><p>A common justification for prohibiting incest is avoiding <a href="/wiki/Inbreeding" title="Inbreeding">inbreeding</a>: a collection of <a href="/wiki/Inbreeding#Genetic_disorders" title="Inbreeding">genetic disorders</a> suffered by the children of parents with a close <a href="/wiki/Coefficient_of_relationship" title="Coefficient of relationship">genetic relationship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WolfDurham2005_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WolfDurham2005-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Such children are at greater risk for congenital disorders, death, and developmental and physical disability, and that risk is proportional to their parents' <a href="/wiki/Coefficient_of_relationship" title="Coefficient of relationship">coefficient of relationship</a>—a measure of how closely the parents are related genetically.<sup id="cite_ref-WolfDurham2005_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WolfDurham2005-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Afzal_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Afzal-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> But cultural anthropologists have noted that inbreeding avoidance cannot form the sole basis for the incest taboo because the boundaries of the incest prohibition vary widely between cultures, and not necessarily in ways that maximize the avoidance of inbreeding.<sup id="cite_ref-WolfDurham2005_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WolfDurham2005-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In some societies, such as those of <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">Ancient Egypt</a>, brother–sister, father–daughter, mother–son, cousin–cousin, aunt–nephew, uncle–niece, and other combinations of relations within a <a href="/wiki/Royal_family" title="Royal family">royal family</a> were married as a means of perpetuating the royal lineage.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Some societies, such as the <a href="/wiki/Balinese_people" title="Balinese people">Balinese</a><sup id="cite_ref-Bateson_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bateson-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> and some <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a> tribes,<sup id="cite_ref-JBriggs_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JBriggs-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> have different views about what constitutes illegal or immoral incest. However, sexual relations with a first-degree relative (meaning a parent or sibling) are almost universally forbidden.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

</li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#Prevalence_and_statistics"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Prevalence and statistics</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7"><a href="#Types"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Types</span></a>
<ul>
<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8"><a href="#Between_adults_and_children"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Between adults and children</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#Between_childhood_siblings"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Between childhood siblings</span></a></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminology">Terminology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Terminology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Table_of_Consanguinity_showing_degrees_of_relationship.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Table_of_Consanguinity_showing_degrees_of_relationship.svg/290px-Table_of_Consanguinity_showing_degrees_of_relationship.svg.png" decoding="async" width="290" height="261" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Table_of_Consanguinity_showing_degrees_of_relationship.svg/435px-Table_of_Consanguinity_showing_degrees_of_relationship.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Table_of_Consanguinity_showing_degrees_of_relationship.svg/580px-Table_of_Consanguinity_showing_degrees_of_relationship.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="461" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Table_of_Consanguinity_showing_degrees_of_relationship.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The number next to each box indicates the degree of relationship relative to the given person.</div></div></div>
<p>The English word <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/incest" class="extiw" title="wikt:incest">incest</a></i> is derived from the Latin <i>incestus</i>, which has a general meaning of "impure, unchaste".
It was introduced into <a href="/wiki/Middle_English" title="Middle English">Middle English</a>, both in the generic Latin sense (preserved throughout the Middle English period<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>) and in the narrow modern sense.
The derived adjective <i>incestuous</i> appears in the 16th century.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
Before the Latin term came in, incest was known in <a href="/wiki/Old_English" title="Old English">Old English</a> as <i>sib-leger</i> (from <i>sibb</i> 'kinship' + <i>leger</i> 'to lie') or <i>mǣġhǣmed</i> (from <i>mǣġ</i> 'kin, parent' + <i>hǣmed</i> 'sexual intercourse') but in time, both words fell out of use. Terms like <i>incester</i><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> and <i>incestual</i><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> have been used to describe those interested or involved in sexual relations with relatives among humans, while <i>inbreeder</i> has been used in relation to similar behavior among non-human animals or organisms.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other words that describe sexual attraction to relatives include consanguinophilia, consanguinamory, synegenesophilia, incestuality and incestophilia.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-aggrawal_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aggrawal-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:327px;"><a href="/wiki/File:W.Clerke_table.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/W.Clerke_table.PNG/325px-W.Clerke_table.PNG" decoding="async" width="325" height="437" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d3/W.Clerke_table.PNG 1.5x" data-file-width="434" data-file-height="584" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:W.Clerke_table.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Table of prohibited marriages from <i>The Trial of Bastardie</i> by <a href="/wiki/William_Clerke_(writer)" title="William Clerke (writer)">William Clerke</a>. London, 1594</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Antiquity">Antiquity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Antiquity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Ancient_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient China">ancient China</a>, first cousins with the same surnames (i.e., those born to the father's brothers) were not permitted to marry, while those with different surnames could marry.(i.e., maternal cousins and paternal cousins born to the father's sisters) were.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Several of the Egyptian <a href="/wiki/Pharaoh" title="Pharaoh">Pharaohs</a> married their siblings and had several children with them. For example, <a href="/wiki/Tutankhamun" title="Tutankhamun">Tutankhamun</a> married his half-sister <a href="/wiki/Ankhesenamun" title="Ankhesenamun">Ankhesenamun</a>, and was himself the child of an incestuous union between <a href="/wiki/Akhenaten" title="Akhenaten">Akhenaten</a> and an unidentified sister-wife. Several scholars, such as Frier et al., state that sibling marriages were widespread among all classes in Egypt during the Graeco-Roman period. Numerous <a href="/wiki/Papyrus" title="Papyrus">papyri</a> and the Roman census declarations attest to many husbands and wives being brother and sister, of the same father and mother.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> However, it has also been argued that available evidence does not support the view such relations were common.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
The most famous of these relationships were in the <a href="/wiki/Ptolemaic_Kingdom#Ptolemaic_rulers" title="Ptolemaic Kingdom">Ptolemaic royal family</a>; <a href="/wiki/Cleopatra_VII" class="mw-redirect" title="Cleopatra VII">Cleopatra VII</a> was married to her younger brother, <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy_XIII" class="mw-redirect" title="Ptolemy XIII">Ptolemy XIII</a>, while her mother and father, <a href="/wiki/Cleopatra_V_of_Egypt" title="Cleopatra V of Egypt">Cleopatra V</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy_XII" class="mw-redirect" title="Ptolemy XII">Ptolemy XII</a>, had also been brother and sister.
</p><p>The fable of <i><a href="/wiki/Oedipus" title="Oedipus">Oedipus</a></i>, with a theme of inadvertent incest between a mother and son, ends in disaster and shows ancient taboos against incest as Oedipus blinds himself in disgust and shame after his incestuous actions. In the "sequel" to Oedipus, <i><a href="/wiki/Antigone" title="Antigone">Antigone</a></i>, his four children are also punished for their parents' incestuousness. Incest appears in the commonly accepted version of the birth of <a href="/wiki/Adonis" title="Adonis">Adonis</a>, when his mother, <a href="/wiki/Myrrha" title="Myrrha">Myrrha</a> has sex with her father <a href="/wiki/Cinyras" title="Cinyras">Cinyras</a> during a festival, disguised as a prostitute.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Ancient Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Sparta" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient Sparta">Spartan King</a> <a href="/wiki/Leonidas_I" title="Leonidas I">Leonidas I</a>, hero of the legendary <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Thermopylae" title="Battle of Thermopylae">Battle of Thermopylae</a>, was married to his <a href="/wiki/Niece" class="mw-redirect" title="Niece">niece</a> <a href="/wiki/Gorgo,_Queen_of_Sparta" title="Gorgo, Queen of Sparta">Gorgo</a>, daughter of his half-brother <a href="/wiki/Cleomenes_I" title="Cleomenes I">Cleomenes I</a>. Greek law allowed marriage between a brother and sister if they had different mothers. For example, some accounts say that <a href="/wiki/Elpinice" title="Elpinice">Elpinice</a> was for a time married to her half-brother <a href="/wiki/Cimon" title="Cimon">Cimon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Incest is mentioned and condemned in <a href="/wiki/Virgil" title="Virgil">Virgil</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Aeneid" title="Aeneid">Aeneid</a></i> Book VI:<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> <i>hic thalamum invasit natae vetitosque hymenaeos;</i> "This one invaded a daughter's room and a forbidden sex act".
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Yaxchil%C3%A1n_lintel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Yaxchil%C3%A1n_lintel.jpg/190px-Yaxchil%C3%A1n_lintel.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Yaxchil%C3%A1n_lintel.jpg/285px-Yaxchil%C3%A1n_lintel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/53/Yaxchil%C3%A1n_lintel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="343" data-file-height="460" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Yaxchil%C3%A1n_lintel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Maya king <a href="/wiki/Itzamnaaj_B%27alam_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Itzamnaaj B&#39;alam II">Shield Jaguar II</a> with his <a href="/wiki/Avunculate_marriage" title="Avunculate marriage">aunt-wife</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lady_Xoc" title="Lady Xoc">Lady Xoc</a>. AD 709</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Roman_law" title="Roman law">Roman civil law</a> prohibited marriages within four degrees of consanguinity<sup id="cite_ref-SRCL514_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SRCL514-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> but had no degrees of affinity with regards to marriage. Roman civil laws prohibited any marriage between parents and children, either in the ascending or descending line <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ad_infinitum" class="extiw" title="wikt:ad infinitum"><i>ad infinitum</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SRCL514_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SRCL514-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Adoption was considered the same as affinity in that an adoptive father could not marry an <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/unemancipated" class="extiw" title="wikt:unemancipated">unemancipated</a> daughter or granddaughter even if the adoption had been dissolved.<sup id="cite_ref-SRCL514_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SRCL514-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Incestuous unions were discouraged and considered <i><a href="/wiki/Nefas" class="mw-redirect" title="Nefas">nefas</a></i> (against the laws of gods and man) in <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">ancient Rome</a>. In AD 295 incest was explicitly forbidden by an imperial edict, which divided the concept of <i>incestus</i> into two categories of unequal gravity: the <i>incestus iuris gentium,</i> which was applied to both Romans and non-Romans in the Empire, and the <i>incestus iuris civilis,</i> which concerned only Roman citizens. Therefore, for example, an Egyptian could marry an aunt, but a Roman could not. Despite the act of incest being unacceptable within the Roman Empire, Roman Emperor <a href="/wiki/Caligula" title="Caligula">Caligula</a> is rumored to have had sexual relationships with all three of his sisters (<a href="/wiki/Julia_Livilla" title="Julia Livilla">Julia Livilla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drusilla_(sister_of_Caligula)" class="mw-redirect" title="Drusilla (sister of Caligula)">Drusilla</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Agrippina_the_Younger" title="Agrippina the Younger">Agrippina the Younger</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Emperor <a href="/wiki/Claudius" title="Claudius">Claudius</a>, after executing his previous wife, married his brother's daughter Agrippina the Younger, and changed the law to allow an otherwise illegal union.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The law prohibiting marrying a sister's daughter remained.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The taboo against incest in Ancient Rome is demonstrated by the fact that politicians would use charges of incest (often false charges) as insults and means of political disenfranchisement.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Norse_mythology" title="Norse mythology">Norse mythology</a>, there are themes of brother-sister marriage, a prominent example being between <a href="/wiki/Nj%C3%B6r%C3%B0r" title="Njörðr">Njörðr</a> and his <a href="/wiki/Sister-wife_of_Nj%C3%B6r%C3%B0r" title="Sister-wife of Njörðr">unnamed sister</a> (perhaps <a href="/wiki/Nerthus" title="Nerthus">Nerthus</a>), parents of <a href="/wiki/Freyja" title="Freyja">Freyja</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freyr" title="Freyr">Freyr</a>. <a href="/wiki/Loki" title="Loki">Loki</a> in turn also accuses Freyja and Freyr of having a sexual relationship.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biblical_references">Biblical references</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Biblical references">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The earliest Biblical reference to incest involved Cain. It was cited that he knew his wife and she conceived and bare Enoch.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> During this period, there was no other woman except Eve or there was an unnamed sister and so this meant Cain had incestuous relationship with his mother or his sister.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Jubilees" title="Book of Jubilees">Book of Jubilees</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cain" class="mw-redirect" title="Cain">Cain</a> married his sister <a href="/wiki/Awan_(religious_figure)" title="Awan (religious figure)">Awan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Later, in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.mechon-mamre.org/p/pt/pt0120.htm#12">Genesis 20:12</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_Bible" title="Hebrew Bible">Hebrew Bible</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Patriarch" title="Patriarch">Patriarch</a> <a href="/wiki/Abraham" title="Abraham">Abraham</a> married his half-sister <a href="/wiki/Sarah" title="Sarah">Sarah</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESka200926–31_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESka200926–31-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Other references include the passage in Samuel where <a href="/wiki/Amnon" title="Amnon">Amnon</a>, King <a href="/wiki/David" title="David">David</a>'s son, raped his half-sister, <a href="/wiki/Tamar_(2_Samuel)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tamar (2 Samuel)">Tamar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Michael_D._Coogan" class="mw-redirect" title="Michael D. Coogan">Michael D. Coogan</a>, it would have been perfectly all right for Amnon to have married her (the Bible being incoherent about prohibiting incest).<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Genesis 19:30-38, living in an isolated area after the destruction of <a href="/wiki/Sodom_and_Gomorrah" title="Sodom and Gomorrah">Sodom and Gomorrah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lot_(biblical_person)" title="Lot (biblical person)">Lot</a>'s two daughters conspired to inebriate and seduce their father due to the lack of available partners to continue his <a href="/wiki/Lineage_(anthropology)" title="Lineage (anthropology)">line of descent</a>. Because of intoxication, Lot "perceived not" when his firstborn, and the following night his younger daughter, lay with him (Genesis 19:32-35). 
</p><p>Moses was also born to an incestuous marriage. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.mechon-mamre.org/p/pt/pt0206.htm#20">Exodus 6:20</a> detailed how his father <a href="/wiki/Amram" title="Amram">Amram</a> was the nephew of his mother <a href="/wiki/Jochebed" title="Jochebed">Jochebed</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> An account noted that the incestuous relations did not suffer the fate of childlessness, which was the punishment for such couples in levitical law.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> It stated, however, that the incest exposed Moses "to the peril of wild beasts, of the weather, of the water, and more."<sup id="cite_ref-:2_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="From_the_Middle_Ages_onward">From the Middle Ages onward</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: From the Middle Ages onward">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rey_Carlos_II.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Rey_Carlos_II.jpg/220px-Rey_Carlos_II.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="259" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Rey_Carlos_II.jpg/330px-Rey_Carlos_II.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Rey_Carlos_II.jpg/440px-Rey_Carlos_II.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1855" data-file-height="2184" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rey_Carlos_II.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_Spain" title="Charles II of Spain">Charles II of Spain</a> was born mentally and physically disabled due to centuries of inbreeding in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">House of Habsburg</a></div></div></div>
<p>Many European monarchs were related due to political marriages, sometimes resulting in distant cousins (and even first cousins) being married. This was especially true in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">Habsburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/House_of_Hohenzollern" title="House of Hohenzollern">Hohenzollern</a>, <a href="/wiki/House_of_Savoy" title="House of Savoy">Savoy</a> and <a href="/wiki/House_of_Bourbon" title="House of Bourbon">Bourbon</a> royal houses. However, relations between siblings, which may have been tolerated in other cultures, were considered abhorrent. For example, the accusation that <a href="/wiki/Anne_Boleyn" title="Anne Boleyn">Anne Boleyn</a> and her brother <a href="/wiki/George_Boleyn,_2nd_Viscount_Rochford" title="George Boleyn, 2nd Viscount Rochford">George Boleyn</a> had committed incest was one of the reasons that both siblings were executed in May 1536.
</p><p>Incestuous marriages were also seen in the royal houses of ancient <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> and Korea,<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Inca <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Hawaii" title="Ancient Hawaii">Ancient Hawaii</a>, and, at times, Central Africa, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Like the pharaohs of ancient Egypt, the <a href="/wiki/Inca" class="mw-redirect" title="Inca">Inca</a> rulers married their sisters. <a href="/wiki/Huayna_Capac" title="Huayna Capac">Huayna Capac</a>, for instance, was the son of <a href="/wiki/Topa_Inca_Yupanqui" title="Topa Inca Yupanqui">Topa Inca Yupanqui</a> and the Inca's sister and wife.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Half-sibling marriages were found in ancient Japan such as the marriage of <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Bidatsu" title="Emperor Bidatsu">Emperor Bidatsu</a> and his half-sister <a href="/wiki/Empress_Suiko" title="Empress Suiko">Empress Suiko</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Japanese <a href="/wiki/Prince_Kinashi_no_Karu" title="Prince Kinashi no Karu">Prince Kinashi no Karu</a> had sexual relationships with his full sister Princess Karu no Ōiratsume, although the action was regarded as foolish.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> In order to prevent the influence of the other families, a half-sister of Korean <a href="/wiki/Goryeo" title="Goryeo">Goryeo</a> Dynasty monarch <a href="/wiki/Gwangjong_of_Goryeo" title="Gwangjong of Goryeo">Gwangjong</a> became his wife in the 10th century. Her name was Daemok.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Marriage with a family member not related by blood was also regarded as contravening morality and was therefore incest. One example of this is the 14th century <a href="/wiki/Chunghye_of_Goryeo" title="Chunghye of Goryeo">Chunghye of Goryeo</a>, who raped one of his deceased <a href="/wiki/Princess_Gyeonghwa" title="Princess Gyeonghwa">father's concubines</a>, who was thus regarded to be his mother.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In India, the largest proportion of women aged 13–49 who marry their close relative are in <a href="/wiki/Tamil_Nadu" title="Tamil Nadu">Tamil Nadu</a>, then <a href="/wiki/Andhra_Pradesh" title="Andhra Pradesh">Andhra Pradesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karnataka" title="Karnataka">Karnataka</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Maharashtra" title="Maharashtra">Maharashtra</a>. While it is rare for uncle-niece marriages, it is more common in <a href="/wiki/Andhra_Pradesh" title="Andhra Pradesh">Andhra Pradesh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tamil_Nadu" title="Tamil Nadu">Tamil Nadu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Prevalence_and_statistics">Prevalence and statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Prevalence and statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Incest between an adult and a person under the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_consent" title="Age of consent">age of consent</a> is considered a form of <a href="/wiki/Child_sexual_abuse" title="Child sexual abuse">child sexual abuse</a><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> that has been shown to be one of the most extreme forms of childhood abuse; it often results in serious and long-term <a href="/wiki/Psychological_trauma" title="Psychological trauma">psychological trauma</a>, especially in the case of parental incest.<sup id="cite_ref-Courtois_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Courtois-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Its prevalence is difficult to generalize, but research has estimated 10–15% of the general population as having at least one such sexual contact, with less than 2% involving intercourse or attempted intercourse.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Among women, research has yielded estimates as high as 20%.<sup id="cite_ref-Courtois_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Courtois-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Father" title="Father">Father</a>–<a href="/wiki/Daughter" title="Daughter">daughter</a> incest was for many years the most commonly reported and studied form of incest.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Herman_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Herman-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> More recently, studies have suggested that <a href="/wiki/Sibling_incest" class="mw-redirect" title="Sibling incest">sibling incest</a>, particularly older brothers having sexual relations with younger siblings, is the most common form of incest,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> with some studies finding sibling incest occurring more frequently than other forms of incest.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Some studies suggest that adolescent perpetrators of sibling abuse choose younger victims, abuse victims over a lengthier period, use violence more frequently and severely than adult perpetrators, and that sibling abuse has a higher rate of penetrative acts than father or stepfather incest, with father and older brother incest resulting in greater reported distress than stepfather incest.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Types">Types</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Types">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Between_adults_and_children">Between adults and children</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Between adults and children">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Child_sexual_abuse" title="Child sexual abuse">Child sexual abuse</a></div>
<p>Sex between an adult family member and a child is usually considered a form of child sexual abuse,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> also known as <b>child incestuous abuse</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> and for many years has been the most reported form of incest. Father–daughter and stepfather–stepdaughter sex is the most commonly reported form of adult–child incest, with most of the remaining involving a mother or stepmother.<sup id="cite_ref-Turner_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turner-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Many studies found that stepfathers tend to be far more likely than biological fathers to engage in this form of incest. One study of adult women in San Francisco estimated that 17% of women were abused by stepfathers and 2% were abused by biological fathers.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Father–son incest is reported less often, but it is not known how close the frequency is to heterosexual incest because it is likely more under-reported.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Prevalence of incest between parents and their children is difficult to assess due to secrecy and privacy.
</p><p>In a 1999 news story, <i>BBC</i> reported, "Close-knit family life in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> masks an alarming amount of sexual abuse of children and teenage girls by family members, a new report suggests. Delhi organisation <a href="/wiki/RAHI_Foundation" title="RAHI Foundation">RAHI</a> said 76% of respondents to its survey had been abused when they were children—40% of those by a family member."<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the National Center for Victims of Crime a large proportion of <a href="/wiki/Rape" title="Rape">rape</a> committed in the United States is perpetrated by a family member:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Research indicates that 46% of children who are raped are victims of family members (Langan and Harlow, 1994). The majority of American rape victims (61%) are raped before the age of 18; furthermore, 29% of all rapes occurred when the victim was less than 11 years old. 11% of rape victims are raped by their fathers or stepfathers, and another 16% are raped by other relatives<i>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup></i>
</p></blockquote>
<p>A study of victims of father–daughter incest in the 1970s showed that there were "common features" within families before the occurrence of incest: estrangement between the mother and the daughter, extreme paternal dominance, and reassignment of some of the mother's traditional major family responsibility to the daughter. Oldest and only daughters were more likely to be the victims of incest. It was also stated that the incest experience was psychologically harmful to the woman in later life, frequently leading to feelings of low self-esteem, very unhealthy sexual activity, contempt for other women, and other emotional problems.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (July 2009)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Adults who as children were incestuously victimized by adults often suffer from low <a href="/wiki/Self-esteem" title="Self-esteem">self-esteem</a>, difficulties in interpersonal relationships, and <a href="/wiki/Sexual_dysfunction" title="Sexual dysfunction">sexual dysfunction</a>, and are at an extremely high risk of many mental disorders, including <a href="/wiki/Clinical_depression" class="mw-redirect" title="Clinical depression">depression</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anxiety_disorder" title="Anxiety disorder">anxiety disorders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phobia" title="Phobia">phobic avoidance reactions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somatoform_disorder" class="mw-redirect" title="Somatoform disorder">somatoform disorder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Substance_abuse" title="Substance abuse">substance abuse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Borderline_personality_disorder" title="Borderline personality disorder">borderline personality disorder</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Complex_post-traumatic_stress_disorder" title="Complex post-traumatic stress disorder">complex post-traumatic stress disorder</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Courtois_63-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Courtois-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Goler_clan" title="Goler clan">Goler clan</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a> is a specific instance in which child sexual abuse in the form of forced adult/child and sibling/sibling incest took place over at least three generations.<sup id="cite_ref-cruise_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cruise-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>  A number of Goler children were victims of sexual abuse at the hands of fathers, mothers, uncles, aunts, sisters, brothers, cousins, and each other. During interrogation by police, several of the adults openly admitted to engaging in many forms of sexual activity, up to and including full intercourse, multiple times with the children. Sixteen adults (both men and women) were charged with hundreds of allegations of incest and sexual abuse of children as young as five.<sup id="cite_ref-cruise_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cruise-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> In July 2012, twelve children were removed from the <a href="/wiki/Colt_clan_incest_case" title="Colt clan incest case">'Colt' family</a> (a pseudonym) in <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a>, Australia, after the discovery of four generations of incest.<sup id="cite_ref-ccnsw_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ccnsw-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nca131210_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nca131210-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Child protection workers and psychologists said interviews with the children indicated "a virtual sexual free-for-all".<sup id="cite_ref-nca131212_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nca131212-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Japan, there is a popular misconception that mother-son incestuous contact is common, due to the manner in which it is depicted in the press and popular media. According to Hideo Tokuoka, "When Americans think of incest, they think of fathers and daughters; in Japan one thinks of mothers and sons" due to the extensive media coverage of mother-son incest there.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Some western researchers assumed that mother-son incest is common in Japan, but research into victimization statistics from police and health-care systems discredits this; it shows that the vast majority of sexual abuse, including incest, in Japan is perpetrated by men against young girls.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While incest between adults and children generally involves the adult as the perpetrator of abuse, there are rare instances of sons sexually assaulting their mothers. These sons are typically mid adolescent to young adult, and, unlike parent-initiated incest, the incidents involve some kind of physical force. Although the mothers may be accused of being seductive with their sons and inviting the sexual contact, this is contrary to evidence.<sup id="cite_ref-Courtois_2_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Courtois_2-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ward_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ward-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Such accusations can parallel other forms of rape, where, due to <a href="/wiki/Victim_blaming" title="Victim blaming">victim blaming</a>, a woman is accused of somehow being at fault for the rape. In some cases, mother-son incest is best classified as <a href="/wiki/Acquaintance_rape" title="Acquaintance rape">acquaintance rape</a> of the mother by the adolescent son.<sup id="cite_ref-Courtois_2_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Courtois_2-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ward_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ward-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Between_childhood_siblings">Between childhood siblings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Between childhood siblings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Childhood <a href="/wiki/Sibling_incest" class="mw-redirect" title="Sibling incest">sibling–sibling incest</a> is considered to be widespread but rarely reported.<sup id="cite_ref-Turner_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turner-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Sibling–sibling incest becomes <a href="/wiki/Child-on-child_sexual_abuse" title="Child-on-child sexual abuse">child-on-child sexual abuse</a> when it occurs without consent, without equality, or as a result of <a href="/wiki/Coercion" title="Coercion">coercion</a>. In this form, it is believed to be the most common form of intrafamilial abuse.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> The most commonly reported form of abusive sibling incest is abuse of a younger sibling by an older sibling.<sup id="cite_ref-Turner_82-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turner-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> A 2006 study showed a large portion of adults who experienced sibling incest abuse have "distorted" or "disturbed" beliefs (such as that the act was "normal") both about their own experience and the subject of sexual abuse in general.<sup id="cite_ref-Carlson_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carlson-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sibling abusive incest is most prevalent in families where one or both parents are often absent or emotionally unavailable, with the abusive siblings using incest as a way to assert their power over a weaker sibling.<sup id="cite_ref-leder_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leder-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Absence of the father in particular has been found to be a significant element of most cases of sexual abuse of female children by a brother.<sup id="cite_ref-rudd_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rudd-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> The damaging effects on both childhood development and adult symptoms resulting from brother–sister sexual abuse are similar to the effects of father–daughter, including substance abuse, depression, suicidality, and eating disorders.<sup id="cite_ref-rudd_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rudd-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cyr_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cyr-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Between_consenting_adults">Between consenting adults</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Between consenting adults">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sexual activity between adult close relatives is sometimes ascribed to <a href="/wiki/Genetic_sexual_attraction" title="Genetic sexual attraction">genetic sexual attraction</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian2002_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian2002-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> This form of incest has not been widely reported, but evidence has indicated that this behavior does take place, possibly more often than many people realize.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian2002_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian2002-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Internet <a href="/wiki/Chatroom" class="mw-redirect" title="Chatroom">chatrooms</a> and topical websites exist that provide support for incestuous couples.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian2002_106-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian2002-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Proponents of incest between consenting adults draw clear boundaries between the behavior of consenting adults and rape, child molestation, and abusive incest.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian2002_106-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian2002-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> However, even consensual relationships such as these are still legally classified as incest,<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> and criminalized in many jurisdictions <span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">(see <a href="/wiki/Laws_regarding_incest" class="mw-redirect" title="Laws regarding incest">Laws regarding incest</a> for exceptions)</span>. James Roffee, a senior lecturer in criminology at <a href="/wiki/Monash_University" title="Monash University">Monash University</a> and former worker on legal responses to familial sexual activity in England and Wales, and Scotland,<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> discussed how the European Convention on Human Rights deems all familial sexual acts to be criminal, even if all parties give their full consent and are knowledgeable to all possible consequences.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> He also argues that the use of particular language tools in the legislation manipulates the reader to deem all familial sexual activities as immoral and criminal, even if all parties are consenting adults.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to one incest participant who was quoted for an article in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047036"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>You can't help who you fall in love with, it just happens. I fell in love with my sister and I'm not ashamed ... I only feel sorry for my mom and dad, I wish they could be happy for us. We love each other. It's nothing like some old man who tries to fuck his three-year-old, that's evil and disgusting ... Of course we're consenting, that's the most important thing. We're not fucking perverts. What we have is the most beautiful thing in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian2002_106-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian2002-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>In <i><a href="/wiki/Slate_(magazine)" title="Slate (magazine)">Slate</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/William_Saletan" title="William Saletan">William Saletan</a> drew a legal connection between gay sex and incest between consenting adults.<sup id="cite_ref-slate2003_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-slate2003-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> As he described in his article, in 2003, U.S. Senator <a href="/wiki/Rick_Santorum" title="Rick Santorum">Rick Santorum</a> commented on a pending U.S. Supreme Court case involving sodomy laws (primarily as a matter of <a href="/wiki/Civil_and_political_rights" title="Civil and political rights">constitutional rights</a> to <a href="/wiki/Right_to_privacy#United_States" title="Right to privacy">privacy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Equal_Protection_Clause" title="Equal Protection Clause">equal protection under the law</a>):
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047036"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>"If the Supreme Court says that you have the right to consensual sex within your home, then you have the right to bigamy, you have the right to polygamy, you have the right to incest, you have the right to adultery."<sup id="cite_ref-slate2003_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-slate2003-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>Saletan argued that, legally and morally, there is essentially no difference between the two, and went on to support incest between consenting adults being covered by a legal right to privacy.<sup id="cite_ref-slate2003_111-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-slate2003-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/UCLA_School_of_Law" title="UCLA School of Law">UCLA</a> law professor <a href="/wiki/Eugene_Volokh" title="Eugene Volokh">Eugene Volokh</a> has made similar arguments.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> In a more recent article, Saletan said that incest is wrong because it introduces the possibility of irreparably damaging family units by introducing "a notoriously incendiary dynamic—sexual tension—into the mix".<sup id="cite_ref-slt10_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-slt10-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Aunts.2C_uncles.2C_nieces_or_nephews"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Aunts,_uncles,_nieces_or_nephews">Aunts, uncles, nieces or nephews</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Aunts, uncles, nieces or nephews">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Avunculate_marriage" title="Avunculate marriage">Avunculate marriage</a></div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, marrying one's nephew or niece is legal, but only with the explicit permission of the Dutch Government, due to the possible risk of <a href="/wiki/Genetic_defects" class="mw-redirect" title="Genetic defects">genetic defects</a> among the offspring. Nephew-niece marriages predominantly occur among foreign immigrants. In November 2008, the Christian Democratic (CDA) party's Scientific Institute announced that it wanted a ban on marriages to nephews and nieces.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Consensual sex between adults (persons of 18 years and older) is always lawful in the Netherlands and Belgium, even among closely related family members. Sexual acts between an adult family member and a minor are illegal, though they are not classified as incest, but as abuse of the authority such an adult has over a minor, comparable to that of a teacher, coach or priest.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Florida, consensual adult sexual intercourse with someone known to be your aunt, uncle, niece or nephew constitutes a felony of the third degree.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Other states also commonly prohibit marriages between such kin.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> The legality of sex with a half-aunt or half-uncle varies state by state.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the United Kingdom, incest includes only sexual intercourse with a parent, grandparent, child or sibling,<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> but the more recently introduced offence of "sex with an adult relative" extends also as far as half-siblings, uncles, aunts, nephews and nieces.<sup id="cite_ref-ref1_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ref1-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>  However, the term 'incest' remains widely used in popular culture to describe any form of sexual activity with a relative. In Canada, marriage between uncles and nieces and between aunts and nephews is legal.<sup id="cite_ref-can1_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-can1-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Between_adult_siblings">Between adult siblings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Between adult siblings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sibling_incest" class="mw-redirect" title="Sibling incest">Sibling incest</a></div>
<p>The most public case of consensual adult sibling incest in recent years is the case of a brother-sister couple from Germany, <a href="/wiki/Patrick_St%C3%BCbing" title="Patrick Stübing">Patrick Stübing</a> and Susan Karolewski. Because of violent behavior on the part of his father, Patrick was taken in at the age of 3 by foster parents, who adopted him later. At the age of 23 he learned about his biological parents, contacted his mother, and met her and his then 16-year-old sister Susan for the first time. The now-adult Patrick moved in with his birth family shortly thereafter. After their mother died suddenly six months later, the siblings became intimately close, and had their first child together in 2001. By 2004, they had four children together: Eric, Sarah, Nancy, and Sofia. The public nature of their relationship, and the repeated <a href="/wiki/Prosecution" class="mw-redirect" title="Prosecution">prosecutions</a> and even jail time they have served as a result, has caused some in Germany to question whether incest between consenting adults should be punished at all. An article about them in <i><a href="/wiki/Der_Spiegel" title="Der Spiegel">Der Spiegel</a></i> states that the couple are happy together. According to court records, the first three children have mental and physical disabilities, and have been placed in foster care.<sup id="cite_ref-spiegel_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spiegel-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> In April 2012, at the <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Human_Rights" title="European Court of Human Rights">European Court of Human Rights</a>, Patrick Stübing lost his case that the conviction violated his right to a private and family life.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ECtHR_judgment_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECtHR_judgment-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> On September 24, 2014, the <a href="/wiki/German_Ethics_Council" title="German Ethics Council">German Ethics Council</a> has recommended that the government abolish laws criminalizing incest between siblings, arguing that such bans impinge upon citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some societies differentiate between full sibling and half sibling relations. In ancient societies, full sibling and half sibling marriages occurred.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cousin_relationships">Cousin relationships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Cousin relationships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cousin_marriage" title="Cousin marriage">Cousin marriage</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_coupled_cousins" title="List of coupled cousins">List of coupled cousins</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Giuseppe_Arcimboldi_003.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Giuseppe_Arcimboldi_003.jpg/200px-Giuseppe_Arcimboldi_003.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="251" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Giuseppe_Arcimboldi_003.jpg/300px-Giuseppe_Arcimboldi_003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Giuseppe_Arcimboldi_003.jpg/400px-Giuseppe_Arcimboldi_003.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1432" data-file-height="1798" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Giuseppe_Arcimboldi_003.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Maximilian_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Maximilian II, Holy Roman Emperor">Maximilian II, Holy Roman Emperor</a> married his first cousin <a href="/wiki/Maria_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Maria of Spain">Maria of Spain</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Marriages and sexual relationships between first cousins are stigmatized as incest in some cultures, but tolerated in much of the world. Currently, 24 <a href="/wiki/US_states" class="mw-redirect" title="US states">US states</a> prohibit marriages between first cousins, and another seven permit them only under special circumstances.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
The United Kingdom permits both marriage and sexual relations between first cousins.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref1_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref1-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In some non-Western societies, marriages between close biological relatives account for 20% to 60% of all marriages.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>First- and second-cousin marriages are rare, accounting for less than 1% of marriages in Western Europe, North America and Oceania, while reaching 9% in South America, East Asia and South Europe and about 50% in regions of the Middle East, North Africa and South Asia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (June 2017)">dubious</span></a>&#32;<span class="metadata"> &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Talk:Incest#Dubious" title="Talk:Incest">discuss</a></span></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> Communities such as the Dhond and the <a href="/wiki/Bhittani" class="mw-redirect" title="Bhittani">Bhittani</a> of Pakistan clearly prefer marriages between cousins as belief they ensure purity of the descent line, provide intimate knowledge of the spouses, and ensure that <a href="/wiki/Property" title="Property">patrimony</a> will not pass into the hands of "outsiders".<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/Parallel_and_cross_cousins" title="Parallel and cross cousins">Cross-cousin</a> marriages are preferred among the <a href="/wiki/Yanomami" title="Yanomami">Yanomami</a> of Brazilian Amazonia, among many other tribal societies identified by anthropologists.
</p><p>There are some cultures in Asia which stigmatize cousin marriage, in some instances even marriages between second cousins or more remotely related people. This is notably true in the culture of <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a>. In South Korea, before 1997, anyone with the same last name and clan were prohibited from marriage. In light of this law being held unconstitutional, South Korea now only prohibits up to third cousins (see <a href="/wiki/Article_809_of_the_Korean_Civil_Code" title="Article 809 of the Korean Civil Code">Article 809 of the Korean Civil Code</a>). <a href="/wiki/Hmong_people" title="Hmong people">Hmong</a> culture prohibits the marriage of anyone with the same last name – to do so would result in being shunned by the entire community, and they are usually stripped of their last name.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Some <a href="/wiki/Hindu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> communities in India prohibit cousin marriages.
</p><p>In a review of 48 studies on the children parented by cousins, the rate of birth defects was twice that of non-related couples: 4% for cousin couples as opposed to 2% for the general population.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Defined_through_marriage">Defined through marriage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Defined through marriage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Some cultures include relatives by marriage in incest prohibitions; these relationships are called <a href="/wiki/Affinity_(law)" title="Affinity (law)">affinity</a> rather than <a href="/wiki/Consanguinity" title="Consanguinity">consanguinity</a>. For example, the question of the legality and morality of a widower who wished to marry his <a href="/wiki/Deceased_Wife%27s_Sister%27s_Marriage_Act_1907" title="Deceased Wife&#39;s Sister&#39;s Marriage Act 1907">deceased wife's sister</a> was the subject of long and fierce debate in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> in the 19th century, involving, among others, <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Boulton" title="Matthew Boulton">Matthew Boulton</a><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_La_Trobe" title="Charles La Trobe">Charles La Trobe</a>. The marriages were entered into in Scotland and Switzerland respectively, where they were legal. In medieval Europe, standing as a <a href="/wiki/Godparent" title="Godparent">godparent</a> to a child also created a bond of affinity.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> But in other societies, a deceased spouse's sibling was considered the ideal person to marry. The Hebrew Bible forbids a man from marrying his brother's widow with the exception that, if his brother died childless, the man is instead required to marry his brother's widow so as to "raise up seed to him" (per <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.mechon-mamre.org/p/pt/pt0525.htm#5">Deuteronomy 25:5–6</a>).  Some societies have long practiced <a href="/wiki/Sororal_polygyny" class="mw-redirect" title="Sororal polygyny">sororal polygyny</a>, a form of <a href="/wiki/Polygamy" title="Polygamy">polygamy</a> in which a man marries multiple wives who are sisters to each other (though not closely related to him).
</p><p>In Islamic law, marriage among close blood relations like parents, stepparent, parents in-law, siblings, stepsiblings, the children of siblings, aunts and uncles is prohibited, while first or second cousins may marry. Marrying the widow of a brother, or the sister of deceased or divorced wife is also allowed.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Inbreeding">Inbreeding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Inbreeding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Inbreeding" title="Inbreeding">Inbreeding</a></div>
<p>Offspring of biologically related parents are subject to the possible impact of inbreeding. Such offspring have a higher possibility of <a href="/wiki/Congenital_disorder" class="mw-redirect" title="Congenital disorder">congenital birth defects</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Coefficient_of_relationship" title="Coefficient of relationship">Coefficient of relationship</a>) because it increases the proportion of zygotes that are <a href="/wiki/Homozygous" class="mw-redirect" title="Homozygous">homozygous</a> for deleterious <a href="/wiki/Recessive_allele" class="mw-redirect" title="Recessive allele">recessive alleles</a> that produce such disorders<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> (see <a href="/wiki/Inbreeding_depression" title="Inbreeding depression">Inbreeding depression</a>). Because most such <a href="/wiki/Allele" title="Allele">alleles</a> are rare in populations, it is unlikely that two unrelated marriage partners will both be heterozygous carriers. However, because close relatives <a href="/wiki/Coefficient_of_relationship" title="Coefficient of relationship">share a large fraction of their alleles</a>, the probability that any such rare deleterious allele present in the common ancestor will be inherited from both related parents is increased dramatically with respect to non-inbred couples. Contrary to common belief, inbreeding does not in itself alter allele frequencies, but rather increases the relative proportion of homozygotes to heterozygotes. This has two contrary effects.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>In the short term, because incestuous reproduction increases <a href="/wiki/Zygosity" title="Zygosity">zygosity</a>, deleterious recessive alleles will express themselves more frequently, leading to increases in spontaneous abortions of zygotes, perinatal deaths, and postnatal offspring with birth defects.</li>
<li>In the long run, however, because of this increased exposure of deleterious recessive alleles to <a href="/wiki/Natural_selection" title="Natural selection">natural selection</a>, their frequency decreases more rapidly in inbred population, leading to a "healthier" population (with fewer deleterious recessive alleles).</li></ul>
<p>The closer two persons are related, the higher the zygosity, and thus the more severe the biological costs of inbreeding. This fact likely explains why inbreeding between close relatives, such as siblings, is less common than inbreeding between cousins.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There may also be other deleterious effects besides those caused by recessive diseases. Thus, similar <a href="/wiki/Immune_system" title="Immune system">immune systems</a> may be more vulnerable to infectious diseases (see <a href="/wiki/Major_histocompatibility_complex_and_sexual_selection" title="Major histocompatibility complex and sexual selection">Major histocompatibility complex and sexual selection</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-moral_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moral-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 1994 study found a mean excess mortality with inbreeding among first cousins of 4.4%.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Children of parent-child or sibling-sibling unions are at increased risk compared to cousin-cousin unions. Studies suggest that 20-36% of these children will die or have major disability due to the inbreeding.<sup id="cite_ref-WolfDurham2005_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WolfDurham2005-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> A study of 29 offspring resulting from brother-sister or father-daughter incest found that 20 had congenital abnormalities, including four directly attributable to autosomal recessive alleles.<sup id="cite_ref-Baird_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baird-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Laws">Laws</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Laws">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Laws_regarding_incest" class="mw-redirect" title="Laws regarding incest">Laws regarding incest</a></div>
<p>Laws regarding sexual activity between close relatives vary considerably between jurisdictions, and depend on the type of sexual activity and the nature of the family relationship of the parties involved, as well as the age and sex of the parties. Prohibition of incest laws may extend to restrictions on marriage rights, which also vary between jurisdictions. Most jurisdictions prohibit parent-child and sibling marriages, while others also prohibit first-cousin and uncle-niece and aunt-nephew marriages. In most places, incest is illegal, regardless of the ages of the two partners. In other countries, incestuous relationships between consenting adults (with the age varying by location) are permitted, including in the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> is the only country that allows marriage between half-siblings and they must seek government counseling before marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While the legality of consensual incest varies by country, sexual assault committed against a relative is usually seen as a very serious crime. In some legal systems, the fact of a perpetrator being a close relative to the victim constitutes an <a href="/wiki/Aggravating_circumstance" class="mw-redirect" title="Aggravating circumstance">aggravating circumstance</a> in the case of sexual crimes such as <a href="/wiki/Rape" title="Rape">rape</a> and <a href="/wiki/Child_sexual_abuse" title="Child sexual abuse">sexual conduct with a minor</a> – this is the case in <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_views">Religious views</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Religious views">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jewish">Jewish</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Jewish">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jewish_views_on_incest" title="Jewish views on incest">Jewish views on incest</a></div>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Torah" title="Torah">Torah</a>, per <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.mechon-mamre.org/p/pt/pt0318.htm#1">Leviticus 18</a>, "the children of Israel"—Israelite men and women alike—are forbidden from sexual relations between people who are "near of kin" (verse 6), who are defined as:
</p>
<ul><li>Parents and children (verse 7)</li>
<li>Siblings and half siblings (verses 9 and 11). Relationships between these are particularly singled out for a curse in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.mechon-mamre.org/e/et/et0527.htm">Deuteronomy 27</a>, and they are of the only two kinds incestuous relationships that are among the particularly-singled-out relationships—with the other particularly-singled-out relationships being ones of non-incestuous family betrayal (cf. verse 20) and bestiality (cf. verse 21)</li>
<li>Grandparents and grandchildren (verse 10)</li>
<li>Aunts and nephews, uncles and nieces, etc. (verses 12–14).<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> Relationships between these are the second kind of relationships that are particularly singled out for a curse in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.mechon-mamre.org/e/et/et0527.htm">Deuteronomy 27</a>, and the explicit examples of children-in-law and mothers-in-law (verse 23) serves to remind the Israelites that <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.mechon-mamre.org/e/et/et0436.htm">the parents-in-law are also (or at least should be also) the children-in-laws' aunts and uncles</a>:</li></ul>
<blockquote><p>And Moses commanded the children of Israel according to the word of the LORD, saying: 'The tribe of the sons of Joseph speaketh right. This is the thing which the LORD hath commanded concerning the daughters of <a href="/wiki/Zelophehad" class="mw-redirect" title="Zelophehad">Zelophehad</a>, saying: Let them be married to whom they think best; only into the family of the tribe of their father shall they be married. So shall no inheritance of the children of Israel remove from tribe to tribe; for the children of Israel shall cleave every one to the inheritance of the tribe of his fathers. And every daughter, that possesseth an inheritance in any tribe of the children of Israel, shall be wife unto one of the family of the tribe of her father, that the children of Israel may possess every man the inheritance of his fathers. So shall no inheritance remove from one tribe to another tribe; for the tribes of the children of Israel shall cleave each one to its own inheritance.' Even as the LORD commanded Moses, so did the daughters of Zelophehad. For Mahlah, Tirzah, and Hoglah, and Milcah, and Noah, the daughters of Zelophehad, were married unto their father's brothers' sons. (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.mechon-mamre.org/p/pt/pt0318.htm#12">Leviticus 18:12-14</a>)</p></blockquote>
