<p>Incestuous relationships are considered so severe among <a href="/wiki/Chillul_Hashem" title="Chillul Hashem"><i>chillulim HaShem</i></a>, acts which bring shame to the name of God, as to be, along with the other forbidden relationships that are mentioned in Leviticus 18, punishable by death as specified in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.mechon-mamre.org/e/et/et0320.htm">Leviticus 20</a>.
</p><p>In the 4th century BCE, the <a href="/wiki/Soferim" class="mw-redirect" title="Soferim">Soferim</a> (<i>scribes</i>) declared that there were relationships within which marriage constituted incest, in addition to those mentioned by the Torah. These additional relationships were termed <i>seconds</i> (Hebrew: <i>sheniyyot</i>), and included the wives of a man's grandfather and grandson.<sup id="cite_ref-TosYeb23_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TosYeb23-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> The classical rabbis prohibited marriage between a man and any of these <i>seconds</i> of his, on the basis that doing so would act as a <i>safeguard</i> against infringing the biblical incest rules,<sup id="cite_ref-Yeb21a_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yeb21a-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> although there was inconclusive debate about exactly what the limits should be for the definition of <i>seconds</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-JewEncInce_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JewEncInce-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Marriages that are forbidden in the Torah (with the exception of uncle-niece marriages) were regarded by the rabbis of the Middle Ages as invalid – as if they had never occurred;<sup id="cite_ref-EbenezerSA_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EbenezerSA-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> any children born to such a couple were regarded as <a href="/wiki/Mamzer" title="Mamzer">bastards under Jewish law</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-EbenezerSA_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EbenezerSA-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> and the relatives of the spouse were not regarded as forbidden relations for a further marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> On the other hand, those relationships which were prohibited due to qualifying as <i>seconds</i>, and so forth, were regarded as wicked, but still valid;<sup id="cite_ref-EbenezerSA_151-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EbenezerSA-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> while they might have pressured such a couple to divorce, any children of the union were still seen as legitimate.<sup id="cite_ref-EbenezerSA_151-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EbenezerSA-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Christian">Christian</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Christian">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> regards incest as a sin against the <a href="/wiki/Marriage_in_the_Catholic_Church" title="Marriage in the Catholic Church">Sacrament of Matrimony</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> For the Catholic Church, at the heart of the immorality of incest is the corruption and disordering of proper family relations. These disordered relationships take on a particularly grave and immoral character when it becomes <a href="/wiki/Child_sexual_abuse" title="Child sexual abuse">child sexual abuse</a>. 
</p><p>
As the <a href="/wiki/Catechism_of_the_Catholic_Church" title="Catechism of the Catholic Church"><i>Catechism of the Catholic Church</i></a> says: </p><blockquote><p><b>2388</b>  <i>Incest</i> designates intimate relations between relatives or in-laws within a degree that prohibits marriage between them. St. Paul stigmatizes this especially grave offense: 'It is actually reported that there is immorality among you...for a man is living with his father's wife....In the name of the Lord Jesus...you are to deliver this man to Satan for the destruction of the flesh....' Incest corrupts family relationships and marks a regression toward animality.
</p><p><br />
</p>
<p><b>2389</b>  Connected to incest is any sexual abuse perpetrated by adults on children or adolescents entrusted to their care. The offense is compounded by the scandalous harm done to the physical and moral integrity of the young, who will remain scarred by it all their lives; and the violation of responsibility for their upbringing.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote> 
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Common_Prayer" title="Book of Common Prayer">Book of Common Prayer</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Communion" title="Anglican Communion">Anglican Communion</a> allows marriages up to and including first cousins.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Islamic">Islamic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Islamic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mahram" title="Mahram">Mahram</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Quran" title="Quran">Quran</a> gives specific rules regarding incest, which prohibit a man from marrying or having sexual relationships with:
</p>
<center>
<table class="wikitable">
<tbody><tr>
<td>
<ul><li>his father's wife<sup id="cite_ref-Quran22_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quran22-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> (his mother,<sup id="cite_ref-Quran23_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quran23-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> or stepmother<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>), his mother-in-law, a woman from whom he has nursed, even the children of this woman<sup id="cite_ref-Quran23_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quran23-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>either parent's sister (aunt),<sup id="cite_ref-Quran23_157-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quran23-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>his sister, his half sister, a woman who has nursed from the same woman as he, his sister-in-law (wife's sister) while still married. Half relations are as sacred as are the full relations.<sup id="cite_ref-Quran23_157-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quran23-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>his niece (child of sibling),<sup id="cite_ref-Quran23_157-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quran23-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>his daughter, his stepdaughter (if the marriage to her mother had been <a href="/wiki/Consummation" title="Consummation">consummated</a>), his daughter-in-law.<sup id="cite_ref-Quran23_157-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quran23-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
</td></tr></tbody></table></center>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cousin_marriage_in_the_Middle_East" title="Cousin marriage in the Middle East">Cousin marriage</a> finds support in Islamic scriptures and is widespread in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although Islam allows cousin marriage,  there are <a href="/wiki/Hadith" title="Hadith">Hadiths</a> attributed to Muhammad calling for distance from the marriage of relatives.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Zoroastrian">Zoroastrian</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Zoroastrian">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-Expand_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2018</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Persia" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient Persia">Ancient Persia</a>, incest between cousins is a blessed virtue although in some sources incest is believed to be related to that of parent-child or brothers-sisters.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> Under <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrianism</a> both royalty, priestly and commoners practiced incest.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_163-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> This tradition was called Xwedodah<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Avestan_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Avestan language">Avestan</a>: <span lang="ae" dir="rtl">Xᵛaētuuadaθa</span>&#8206;, <small>romanized:&#160;</small><i lang="ae-Latn" title="Avestan-language romanization">Xvaetvadatha</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> The tradition was considered so sacred, that the bodily fluids produced by an incestuous couple were thought to have curative powers.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_163-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> For instance, the <a href="/wiki/Vendidad" title="Vendidad">Vendidad</a> advised corpse-bearers to purify themselves with a mixture of urine of a married incestuous couple.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_163-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Nietzsche" title="Friedrich Nietzsche">Friedrich Nietzsche</a>, in his book <i><a href="/wiki/The_Birth_of_Tragedy" title="The Birth of Tragedy">The Birth of Tragedy</a></i>, cited that among Zoroastrians a wise priest is born only by Xvaetvadatha.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>To what extent Xvaetvadatha was practiced in <a href="/wiki/Sasanian" class="mw-redirect" title="Sasanian">Sasanian</a> Iran and before, especially outside the royal and noble families (“dynastic incest”) and, perhaps, the clergy, and whether practices ascribed to them can be assumed to be characteristic of the general population is not clear. There is a lack of genealogies and census material on the frequency of Xvaetvadatha.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> Evidence from <a href="/wiki/Dura-Europos" title="Dura-Europos">Dura-Europos</a>, however, combined with that of the Jewish and Christian sources citing actual cases under the Sasanians, strengthen the evidence of the Zoroastrian texts.  In the post-Sasanian Zoroastrian literature, Xvaetvadatha is said to refer to marriages between cousins instead, which have always been relatively common.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> It has been observed that such incestuous acts received a great deal of glorification as a religious practice and, in addition to being condemned by foreigners (though the reliability of these accusations is questionable since accusations of incest were a common way of denigrating other groups),<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> were considered a great challenge by its own proponents, with accounts suggesting that four copulations was deemed a rare achievement worthy of eternal salvation. It has been suggested that because taking up incestuous relations was a great personal challenge, seemingly repugnant even to Zoroastrians of the time, that it served as an <a href="/wiki/Honest_signal" class="mw-redirect" title="Honest signal">honest signal</a> of commitment and devotion to religious ideals.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hindu">Hindu</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Hindu">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Rigveda" title="Rigveda">Rigveda</a> regard incest to be "evil".<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> speaks of incest in abhorrent terms. Hindus believe there are both <a href="/wiki/Karmic" class="mw-redirect" title="Karmic">karmic</a> and practical bad effects of incest and thus practice strict rules of both <a href="/wiki/Endogamy" title="Endogamy">endogamy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Exogamy" title="Exogamy">exogamy</a>, in relation to the family tree (<i><a href="/wiki/Gotra" title="Gotra">gotra</a></i>) or bloodline (<i><a href="/wiki/Pravaras" title="Pravaras">Pravara</a></i>).
Marriage within the <i>gotra</i> (<i>swagotra</i> marriages) are banned under the rule of exogamy in the traditional matrimonial system.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> People within the <i>gotra</i> are regarded as kin and marrying such a person would be thought of as incest. Marriage with paternal cousins (a form of <a href="/wiki/Parallel_and_cross_cousins" title="Parallel and cross cousins">parallel-cousin</a> relationship) is strictly prohibited.
</p><p>Although generally marriages between persons having the same <i>gotra</i> are prohibited,<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> how this is defined may vary regionally.
Depending on culture and <a href="/wiki/Indian_caste_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian caste system">caste</a> of the population in the region, marriage may be restricted up to seven generations of <i>gotra</i> of father, mother, and grandmother.  In a few rural areas, marriage is banned within same local community is only allowed with those from outside of the community, as they consider a small village to be like brothers and sisters of one large family. These rules are strictly enforced and a couple breaking them is violently punished sometimes.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Animals">Animals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Animals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Animal_sexual_behavior" class="mw-redirect" title="Animal sexual behavior">Animal sexual behavior</a></div>
<p>Many <a href="/wiki/Mammal" title="Mammal">mammal</a> species, including humanity's closest <a href="/wiki/Primate" title="Primate">primate</a> relatives, tend to avoid mating with close relatives, especially if there are alternative partners available.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> However, some chimpanzees have been recorded attempting to mate with their mothers.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> Male rats have been recorded engaging in mating with their sisters, but they tend to prefer non-related females over their sisters.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Livestock" title="Livestock">Livestock</a> breeders often practice controlled breeding to eliminate undesirable characteristics within a population, which is also coupled with <a href="/wiki/Culling" title="Culling">culling</a> of what is considered unfit offspring, especially when trying to establish a new and desirable trait in the stock.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Insects">Insects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Insects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fruit_flies.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Fruit_flies.jpg/220px-Fruit_flies.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Fruit_flies.jpg/330px-Fruit_flies.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Fruit_flies.jpg/440px-Fruit_flies.jpg 2x" data-file-width="917" data-file-height="691" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fruit_flies.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Drosophila_melanogaster" title="Drosophila melanogaster">Common fruit fly</a> females prefer to mate with their own brothers over unrelated males.<sup id="cite_ref-fruit-flies_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fruit-flies-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bed_bug" title="Bed bug">Bed bugs</a>: <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_State_University" title="North Carolina State University">North Carolina State University</a> found that bed bugs, in contrast to most other insects, tolerate incest and are able to genetically withstand the effects of inbreeding quite well.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
